    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText370394601337790797" style="display:none">Here is the novel that started it all- the first book in J.D. Robb's number-one <i>New York Times</i>-bestselling In Death series, featuring New York homicide detective Lieutenant Eve Dallas and Roarke. <br /><br /> It is the year 2058, and technology now completely rules the world. But New York City Detective Eve Dallas knows that the irresistible impulses of the human heart are still ruled by just one thing: passion. <br /><br /> When a senator's daughter is killed, the secret life of prostitution she'd been leading is revealed. The high-profile case takes Lieutenant Eve Dallas into the rarefied circles of Washington politics and society. Further complicating matters is Eve's growing attraction to Roarke, who is one of the wealthiest and most influential men on the planet, devilishly handsome... and the leading suspect in the investigation.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/448202-does-this-series-need-to-be-read-in-the">Does this series need to be read in the order they were published? Are the Characters connected to the next book in the series. . . just wondering if I need to get them from library in the order they are written.

Thanks a bunch :-) Have not read any of J.D. Robbs books yet. . . have read a lot of good reviews for the suspense, romance, mystery books.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_448202'><a id="like_count_community_question_448202" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/448202?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F479309.Naked_in_Death">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/44824289-barbara-rogers"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442164838i/44824289._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/44824289-barbara-rogers">Barbara Rogers</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would definitely suggest reading them in order. I read one of the later ones first -- and it does read okay as a stand-alone -- but there were so ma<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would definitely suggest reading them in order. I read one of the later ones first -- and it does read okay as a stand-alone -- but there were so many interpersonal relationships that you just don't understand unless you read them in order. I went from the one I started on -- somewhere in the 20's of the series -- back to the very first one and read from the first one forward -- to the one I had read out of order -- and then I re-read that one. It made a big difference to me in those character relationships.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200483719" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200483719?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780786542086" href="/book/show/4408317-naked-in-death">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">romance readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Emily May
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200483719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3609192695597507194">... and I was enjoying it up until too swift of a turn into Romancelandia.<br/><br/>The popularity of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/268602.Naked_in_Death__In_Death___1_' title='Naked in Death (In Death, #1) by J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Naked in Death</a> is completely understandable to me. The attraction here is the same as in the most of urban fantasy IMO. Mystery-solving, some world-building (in this case, futuristic instead of paranormal) - it all is only background noise. What you are actually anticipating is the heroine's hookup with some handsome hunk. (That's what I read urban fantasy for anyway.) And the hunk here is something speci</span>
  <span id="freeText3609192695597507194" style="display:none">... and I was enjoying it up until too swift of a turn into Romancelandia.<br /><br />The popularity of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/268602.Naked_in_Death__In_Death___1_" title="Naked in Death (In Death, #1) by J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">Naked in Death</a> is completely understandable to me. The attraction here is the same as in the most of urban fantasy IMO. Mystery-solving, some world-building (in this case, futuristic instead of paranormal) - it all is only background noise. What you are actually anticipating is the heroine's hookup with some handsome hunk. (That's what I read urban fantasy for anyway.) And the hunk here is something special - (1) he is drowning in money; (2) super hot; (3) has morals; (4) buys the heroine stuff; (5) feeds her; (6) he adores everything about the heroine from the get-go; (7), (8), (9) and (10) HE SPEAKS WITH AN IRISH ACCENT. What's not to like, right?<br /><br />Unfortunately, Roarke never managed to work his magic on me. I thought he was controlling, patronizing, stalkerish even, always forcing Eve out of her comfort zone and himself on her (in that signature way - <i>I am going to make you have the most intense orgasm you've ever had, no matter if you want it or not, because I know what you need better than you </i>). <br /><br />Plus, as I've noted above, the switch from mystery to romance was too early in the book. Quarter in, second meeting, and already "her small, firm breast weighed gloriously in his palm" and "he wanted to forget the patience and control he'd taught himself to live by, and just ravage." This bodice-ripperish language totally killed my mood. At that point, I already knew how it would unfold, with "throbbing," "wetness," "I want you but I can't" and so on.<br /><br />Sorry ladies, but romance is not quite my thing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3609192695597507194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

"We have more of a selection on the plane," he said, then settled back with his coffee.<br>"I bet." The steam rising from her cup smelled like heaven. Eve took a tentative sip -- and nearly moaned.<br>It was real. No simulation made from vegetable concentrate so usual since the depletion of the rain forests in the late twentieth. This was the real thing, ground from rich Columbian beans, singing with caffeine.<br>She sipped again, and could have wept.<br>"Problem?" He enjoyed her reaction immensely, the flutter of the lashes, the faint flush, the darkening of the eyes -- a similar response, he noted, to a woman purring under a man's hands.<br>"Do you know how long it's been since I had real coffee?"<br>He smiled. "No."<br>"Neither do I." Unashamed, she closed her eyes as she lifted the cup again. "You'll have to excuse me, this is a private moment. We'll talk on the plane.”</i>

<div id="review_1797427825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1797427825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15131066952885059892"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514240419i/24759958._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I’d been postponing reading this series for a long time and I’m so glad I finally caved because it was right up my alley. <br/><br/>The thing is, I love murder mysteries and crime-solving books with a touch of romance but the futuristic aspect? Sorry, not my jam. <br/>I don’t like anything futuristic/sci-fi/fantasy related. I never connect to such stories. I don’t know why. Maybe I’m unimaginative and dull. Maybe they scare me.<br/><br/>It’s stupid, I know, but look at it this way. How much older am I than Roar</span>
  <span id="freeText15131066952885059892" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514240419i/24759958._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’d been postponing reading this series for a long time and I’m so glad I finally caved because it was right up my alley. <br><br>The thing is, I love murder mysteries and crime-solving books with a touch of romance but the futuristic aspect? Sorry, not my jam. <br>I don’t like anything futuristic/sci-fi/fantasy related. I never connect to such stories. I don’t know why. Maybe I’m unimaginative and dull. Maybe they scare me.<br><br>It’s stupid, I know, but look at it this way. How much older am I than Roarke? Let’s see. If the story is set in 2058 and he was born in 2023, then I’m… <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514241082ra/24760016.gif" width='400"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Right.<br><br>The good news is, I didn’t need to worry. It wasn’t so bad. The futuristic aspect, I mean. There were a few mentions of badass vehicles and gadgets, strange laws (sin tax, seriously?) and funny global issues but that was pretty much it.<br><br>The bad news is, I had a problem with some of the events. For instance, there are mentions of some major global events that happened in 2016 (the book was written in 1995) which obviously did <i>not</i> happen. Because of that, the story seemed a bit implausible.<br><br>Honestly, I’m worried about mankind and our children’s children. The future world sounds so artificial, cold and impersonal. The only good thing are gadgets and tools like domestic droids that clean your house for you. Now <i>that</i>... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/594491.gif" width='400"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You’ve heard of Roarke, right? Yes, his reputation is <i>well</i> deserved. He’s really <i>that</i> hot. And Eve… I loved her. She's a badass chick. Strong, smart, independent. <br><br>Now I need to read 45 books to catch up on this series. I just hope I won’t binge read the whole series for half of 2018 and then fall into a reading slump of epic proportions.<br><br><b>QUICK REVIEW:</b><br><br>Enjoyment: 3.5/5<br>Writing style: 4/5<br>Storyline: 4/5 <br>Hero: 3/5<br>Heroine: 5/5<br>Secondary characters: 4/5 <br>Hotness/steam: 3/5 <br>Romance: 3/5 <br>Angst: 2/5<br>Darkness level: 2/5<br>Humor: 1/5<br>Depth of the book: 3/5<br>POV: multiple (mostly heroine’s), third person<br>Triggers: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[series of murders (on page), child abuse and rape (off page) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510504825i/24426022._SX540_.jpg" width='400"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472174004" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9413584910618916020">I started this series with a bit of trepidation back in 2015. I knew that JD Robb also wrote as Nora Roberts and I had read another book by Ms Roberts and hated it ... so I was a bit wary about starting the In Death books. But I had heard great things about Roarke. Another reason that put me off reading this series is because he is Irish and, being Irish, if it is not done right, it drives me nuts. But she pulled it off. He is perfection. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492191203i/22492356.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I am already up to book 19 but decided to head back to bo</span>
  <span id="freeText9413584910618916020" style="display:none">I started this series with a bit of trepidation back in 2015. I knew that JD Robb also wrote as Nora Roberts and I had read another book by Ms Roberts and hated it ... so I was a bit wary about starting the In Death books. But I had heard great things about Roarke. Another reason that put me off reading this series is because he is Irish and, being Irish, if it is not done right, it drives me nuts. But she pulled it off. He is perfection. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492191203i/22492356.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I am already up to book 19 but decided to head back to book 1 and do a quick recap of how they met and their initial reactions to each other. OMG. I loved it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>... he turned his head, looked five pews back across the aisle and directly into Eve's eyes. It was surprise that had her fighting not to jolt at that sudden and unexpected punch of power. It was will that kept her from blinking or shifting her gaze. For one humming minute they stared at each other ...</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478281138i/21055336._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You fascinate me, Lieutenant Dallas."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492191203i/22492357.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>We meet Mavis, Feeney, Whitney ... Summerset. Yes, I can see now how they started off on the wrong foot. Bit of a poker up his arse alright, Eve. But you take no shit from him.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Galahad, she thought. Her white knight.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492191203i/22492358._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I highly recommend this series.<br><br><br> <b>
  <i>MY ORIGINAL REVIEW - DECEMBER 2105 ...</i>
</b><br>****************************************<br>Well, they say "practice makes perfect" - would love to know who THEY are. Read Nora Roberts years ago and thought it was the greatest load of shite I had ever read - an Irish themed book - I am Irish so a bit sensitive. So totally avoided her forever. Read some forums on Amazon and GRs about Roarke and Eve and thought who are they - In Death - J. D Robb aka Nora Roberts - NO THANK YOU. But then again I saw that a lot of my GR friends are fans of JD so decided to bite the bullet and jump on the bandwagon.... OKAAAAAY - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/268602.Naked_in_Death__In_Death___1_" title="Naked in Death (In Death, #1) by J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">Naked in Death</a>- freaking loved it. Was this the same woman who wrote about and Irish girl who trained a horse for the Kentucky Derby - cannot even remember the storyline now cos it totally pissed me off. Irish people are not like Darby O'Gill and the Little People or like Tom Cruise and Nicole Kidman in Far and Away or whatever it was ... OK, we see our kids progress through school and improve over the years and definitely Ms Roberts did this. Will I go back and read a Nora Roberts book after this/ Not sure, maybe, probably as I can see a definite improvement in her writing style.... so do not understand how many of you gave <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59815.Irish_Hearts__Irish_Hearts__1___2_" title="Irish Hearts (Irish Hearts #1 &amp; 2) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Irish Hearts</a> such high ratings - us Irish coleens are not as dimwitted or innocent as she was ,,,, Deliver us lord from every evil!!! Now I am totally depressed cos I realise that if I have to read the whole IN DEATH series it is going to cost me a feckin' fortune. Goodnight. 23.20 here in Belgium so time for bed! ..... and if I had known it was set in the future I definitely would not have read it but it totally blends in and you do not notice it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13121412073252851465"><b>
  <i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Jan'19</i>
</b>:<br/><br/>Nora Roberts/J.D. Robb is such a prolific author, and the <i>In Death</i> series is exceptional and incomparable and one of my all-time favorites. After reading all 47 books and eagerly awaiting the 48th book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40122014.Connections_in_Death__In_Death___48_' title='Connections in Death (In Death, #48) by J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Connections in Death</a>, I decided to revisit the beginning. It's still a great crime/mystery/suspense read and Eve and Roarke will forever remain one of the absolute best romantic pairings there is. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>Original read/review</i>
</b>:<br/><br/>5+ stars – Crime/Myste</span>
  <span id="freeText13121412073252851465" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Jan'19</i>
</b>:<br /><br />Nora Roberts/J.D. Robb is such a prolific author, and the <i>In Death</i> series is exceptional and incomparable and one of my all-time favorites. After reading all 47 books and eagerly awaiting the 48th book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40122014.Connections_in_Death__In_Death___48_" title="Connections in Death (In Death, #48) by J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">Connections in Death</a>, I decided to revisit the beginning. It's still a great crime/mystery/suspense read and Eve and Roarke will forever remain one of the absolute best romantic pairings there is. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Original read/review</i>
</b>:<br /><br />5+ stars – Crime/Mystery/Romantic Suspense/Futuristic/Thriller<br /><br />Yes! I've <i>finally</i> read the first book in J.D. Robb's, aka Nora Roberts', vastly popular <i>In Death</i> series, and now I understand why there's 30 books and counting...'cause it's an awesome romantic suspense/futuristic mystery thriller and very addictive. In fact, it's a good thing that I brought the first three books with me on my trip since I wanted to immediately jump into the second book after finishing this. I loved it! And all the flattering Roarke talk is totally justified because he's such a mysteriously delicious, sexy alpha hero! I wasn't convinced that a series could stay interesting and fresh enough with the same characters for 30+ books, but I don't think there could ever be enough of Roarke...he's that yummy!<br /><br />I'm not sure if I need to recommend this since it seems that just about everyone else has already read it, but if you like romantic suspense and/or mystery thrillers and haven't yet read <b>Naked in Death</b>, then I highly suggest it. But be prepared to get hooked on the series! Big 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13121412073252851465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_973490812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/973490812" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/973490812?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20336370-naked-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=bajillionaires">bajillionaires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=creeptastic">creeptastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=jerk-of-my-dreams">jerk-of-my-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=diabolical">diabolical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer973490812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14488965528304734187"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/06/review-naked-in-death-by-j-d-robb.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>For those of you who don't already know, J.D. Robb is an alternate pen name for Nora Roberts. I only read my first Nora Roberts' book about a year ago, and was--to put it mildly--pleasantly surprised. <br/><br/>I'd always <i>ass</i>umed that Roberts wrote cornball Walmart-paperback-romances for-your-grandmother, and when I saw a new book with "Witch" in the title, I figured she had jumped on the paranormal train, but was curious enough to check it out.<br/><br/>It was kind of amazing.<br/><br/>And w</span>
  <span id="freeText14488965528304734187" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/06/review-naked-in-death-by-j-d-robb.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>For those of you who don't already know, J.D. Robb is an alternate pen name for Nora Roberts. I only read my first Nora Roberts' book about a year ago, and was--to put it mildly--pleasantly surprised. <br><br>I'd always <i>ass</i>umed that Roberts wrote cornball Walmart-paperback-romances for-your-grandmother, and when I saw a new book with "Witch" in the title, I figured she had jumped on the paranormal train, but was curious enough to check it out.<br><br>It was kind of amazing.<br><br>And with about 30 seconds of research I discovered that rather than "jumping on the paranormal train," it was more likely that Roberts could be held responsible for making books with paranormal elements marketable in the first place. (&lt;------assumptions make you look stoopid. FYI.)<br><br>I really liked this book. <br><br>BUT. <br><br>The too forceful, borderline abusive love interest whose aggression is attributed to his sheer <i>male</i>ness that I was expecting in my first Roberts' book (b/c '70s - '90s bodice rippers you stole from your grandma's stash when you were a teenager) . . . Well, he was hiding out here all along.<br><br>Roarke Nolastname (*rolls eyes*) is a smoking hot Irish self-made bazillionaire. Say that three times fast. Go ahead. Do it. <br><br>He's also a textbook example of a male with abusive tendencies. I know this for FACT, b/c I volunteered at a battered women's shelter while I was in college, and before a place like that will turn you loose in the facility, they educate you. <br><br>Based on that education, Roarke is one giant Red Flag: he has zero respect for personal space, he makes unilateral decisions about things any rational person understands are not decisions to be made unilaterally, he has fits of temper that involve grabbing, shoving, and shaking . . . Red flags . . . Red flags <em>everywhere</em> . . .<br><br>And maybe that's the difference between a book written a couple of years ago and a book written a couple decades ago. <br><br>B/c NAKED IN DEATH <i>was</i> written nearly twenty years ago . . . <br><br>BUT it takes place in the only slightly distant future (2058, I think). So there's this sometimes interesting/sometimes uncomfortable combination of modern/future ideals and innovations coupled with surprisingly old-fashioned tropes.<br><br>Like how our heroine Eve Dallas is as hard core and strong a female character as I'd expect to find in any recently published SFF or UF novel, who lives in a world with legalized prostitution (gov't regulated and taxed, <em>naturally</em>), but who also falls prey to Red Flag b/c hot DAMN.<br><br>No, seriously. Hot DAMN.<br><br>I fell prey too. Like . . . completely. <br><br>And part of the reason for that is b/c Roberts does such a good job of developing Eve and Roarke that you understand <i>why</i> he's a Red Flag, but know that he'd never actually cross that line (even though your brain and statistics tell you otherwise). They're both damaged, victims of horrific childhoods who were made stronger in the crucible rather than broken. They understand each other better than <i>anyone else</i> ever could. <br><br>For real. You can <i>see</i> it, <i>feel</i> it.<br><br>Eve <i>is</i> the one woman who can change Roarke's playboy emotional detachment, and the fact that she has no intention of doing so only makes it more plausible.<br><br>And that kind of masterful manipulation is what makes the other stuff easier to swallow.<br><br>B/c there is lots of other stuff. LOTS: <br><br>All of the secondaries are flat, stock characters. Instalust, which is believable, crosses the line into instalove, which is <em>not</em>. Eve's a cop; Roarke is a "reformed" criminal mastermind. I could put together a very strong argument that Roarke is the main inspiration for Christian Grey (I considered writing a nontraditional review on that vein, but didn't have the patience to follow through). And there's CORN. Cheesy '90s I'm-too-sexy-for-my-shirt corn:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I thought this vintage would suit you. What it lacks in subtlety . . .” He turned back, offering her a glass. “It makes up for in sensuality.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Ugh. <br><br>Also, if you are <em>particularly</em> sensitive to sexual violation, especially the sexual violation of children, NAKED IN DEATH is not for you. I say <em>particularly</em> b/c pretty much everyone finds the notion upsetting, but as far as this kind of thing goes, it's not too bad. There is only one scene that I would label as graphic and it takes place in the context of an adult remembering past abuse, so if you aren't <em>particularly</em> sensitive, it's not any more unpleasant than any other mystery/thriller with psychos or whack jobs doing psycho/whack job things. <br><br>There are other things as well, but you get the idea. Not that it matters, b/c I LOVED it. If I was making a purely emotional decision about this book, I would be giving it at least four stars. Instead, I'm forcing myself to be rational (b/c the handful of times I've gone with my gut, it's come back to haunt me). <br><br>It's worth mentioning that I'm nearly finished with #6 after starting the series four and half days ago, and that speaks for itself, but I can also say that while IN DEATH remains a series with flaws, there are marked improvements, especially in the area of secondary characters. <br><br>SO. Definitely worth a shot in my humble opinion. If you're intimidated by sci-fi, this is just sci-fi enough to have interesting gadgets and speculative changes in federal laws (like the aforementioned legalized prostitution). ALSO, if you're into audiobooks, definitely, <i>definitely</i> worth a try, especially if you can pick them up from your library, and I'd imagine most would have them considering how popular and long-running this series is. I'm notoriously anti-audiobook (b/c ADD), but I started listening to NAKED IN DEATH while roadtripping, and it easily held my attention b/c just that good.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14488965528304734187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_104464031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104464031" />
    <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"><img alt=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295034921p2/1453659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104464031?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"> Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425220184" href="/book/show/558230.Naked_in_Death">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~* by: </span>
      Ren, and Buggy's and Jasmin's review becoming "Roarke Groupies"
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104464031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18042963823230414672"><b>4 Stars</b> - <i><b>Also reviewed at:</b> <a href='http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/2011/04/naked-in-death-1-death-series-by-j-d.html/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></i><br/><br/>Okay, here’s the quick and dirty... well, sort of. <i>
  <b>Naked In Death</b>
</i> is the first book in the daunting (almost 40 books!!... and still growing) “In Death” series by Nora Roberts, writing as J.D. Robb. I kept putting off reading it, for that very reason. <br/><br/>Though, after recent reviews by Goodreads friends who have joined the growing legion of “Roarke Groupies”, I was most curious to read this book to find out for myself what the fuss is over Roar</span>
  <span id="freeText18042963823230414672" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b> - <i><b>Also reviewed at:</b> <a href="http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/2011/04/naked-in-death-1-death-series-by-j-d.html/" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></i><br><br>Okay, here’s the quick and dirty... well, sort of. <i>
  <b>Naked In Death</b>
</i> is the first book in the daunting (almost 40 books!!... and still growing) “In Death” series by Nora Roberts, writing as J.D. Robb. I kept putting off reading it, for that very reason. <br><br>Though, after recent reviews by Goodreads friends who have joined the growing legion of “Roarke Groupies”, I was most curious to read this book to find out for myself what the fuss is over Roarke. While I do not feel I have reached full “Groupie” status, I think perhaps a badge of “Rookie Groupie” is in order. ^_^<br><br>What is it about Roarke? Well, it’s not just that he is a mysterious, tall, dark and stunningly handsome “bad-boy”, or that he owns like…WHOA! … 20-something % of the world in 2058. It is his intelligence, confidence, drive and determination in getting what he wants - and he wants Eve. And who could resist his oh-so-sweet moments, like with the button and the coffee? *sighs* I won’t say anymore so as not to spoil it for those who have not yet read this book, but fans of the series will know what I’m talking about. ^_~<br><br>I seem to recall, prior to reading this book, people expressing that they didn’t really like Eve. Lt. Eve Dallas reminded me of the character of Charlotte King in the TV series, Private Practice. She is prickly, with a hard shell, and I just knew this had to have been developed as a defence mechanism against some trauma she had suffered previously. What Eve needs is the right touch, à la Roarke. I actually really liked Eve, the tough chick.<br><br>I really liked Eve’s friend, Mavis. She was funny and provided the comic relief in the story, like for example, in the scenes below where Mavis and Eve are discussing Roarke: <br><br><i>‘"Is he good? Stupid question," she said quickly. "You wouldn't have stayed otherwise. Wow, Eve, what got into you? Besides his incredibly energetic c**k?"’ </i><br><br><i>‘"Okay, but can you tell me if he looks as good in person as he does in pictures." <br>"Better," Eve muttered. <br>"Jesus, really?" Mavis moaned and let herself fall onto the sofa. "I think I just had an orgasm."’</i><br><br>Yes, that is the kind of effect that Roarke has. ^_^<br><br>One of the issues I did have with the book was with the futuristic elements. For the most part, I did not actually feel immersed in the “future”, but rather, I very much felt like was reading a contemporary novel with bits of unexpanded and unexplained futuristic things dropped in, eg. references to “AutoChef”, “Glida-Grill” etc. without a bit more of a description of it. I mean, you can guess that this “AutoChef” prepares the food in the future, but do we buy the ingredients and put it in there and then a cooked Spaghetti Bolognese comes out? The “Glida-Grill” I assume is a futuristic New York hot dog stand that glides from place to place rather than being set up on a particular corner? While I didn't want an "info dump", I do wish the author hadn’t just dropped names like that, as it took me out of the story, at times.<br><br>Very briefly, ...speaking of "briefs", if you keep reading you will be rewarded further on... ahem... Right, as I was saying, very briefly, the plot involves Lt. Eve Dallas investigating a series of murders committed in the “old way” using “antique” guns. These are the guns of today, ie. revolvers, magnums, etc. Roarke is one of her suspects and this is how they meet. <i>"Up against the wall, Roarke, spread 'em!"</i> Well, it actually didn't happen like that... LOL <br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed my first “In Death” book and will certainly be reading more - Hey, I want to upgrade to full "Roarke Groupie" status! ^_^ - though I will most definitely be pacing myself. <br><br>My Eve (Morena Baccarin):<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399120361i/9510359.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My Roarke (David Gandy) – Even though Roarke is supposed to have longer hair, I think David Gandy is certainly gorgeous enough and has that teasing “rich bad-boy” look about him to suit Roarke’s personality. Special thanks to Quinn for mentioning him! David was a delicious image to have whilst reading. ^_^<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379747193i/106900._SY540_.jpg" width="330" height="440" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335351i/694315._SY540_.jpg" width="340" height="430" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379747216i/107106._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="260" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And since this is <b><i><u>NAKED</u></i> in Death</b>, the following images of Roarke are...*coughs*...well, a must, obviously. LOL Images kindly supplied by Rane. Special thank you, Rane! ^_^<br><br><b>**WARNING: NOT SAFE FOR WORK!**</b><br><br><a href="http://img111.imagevenue.com/img.php?image=68631_0357_299_122_1172lo.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Roarke - Naked in Bed</a><br><br><b>The Reward, as promised....<br><br>This is Roarke, on his travels, and he can't stop thinking about Eve. He might own a lot of the world ... but what he really wants is ... Eve. OMG, Eve, you lucky, lucky woman!</b><br><br>Video footage: <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EWdINUZZzBs" rel="nofollow noopener">Roarke missing Eve</a><br><br>Of course, one of the richest men in the world would only wear Dolce and Gabbana briefs.<br><br>(Special thanks to my friend, Dina, for the above YUMMYLICIOUS video today!)<br><br><br><i>COPYRIGHT DISCLAIMER: I do not hold the copyright to any of the images used in this review. They are posted to add visuals to the review and for fun. If any of these images are yours and you would like me to remove them, please let me know, and I will do so as soon as possible. If I can identify the copyright, I will do so.</i><br></span>

  </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1720908989" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720908989" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720908989?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720908989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6058538640293269374">This is the first J.D. Robb/Nora Roberts book I have read. I have read glowing reviews about the series, but I was a bit hesitant to start a commitment to it. Then, I have come upon a verse from one of the books:<br/> <br/><i>"Oh, but it is you, darling Eve. Just as that taste is you, the smell, the look, the sound. You've undone me." </i><br/><br/>- "Glory in Death"<br/><br/>I think it was devastatingly beautiful! The object of Eve's undoing piqued my interest, so I went on and borrowed the first 2 books.<br/><br/>"Naked in Death" is about </span>
  <span id="freeText6058538640293269374" style="display:none">This is the first J.D. Robb/Nora Roberts book I have read. I have read glowing reviews about the series, but I was a bit hesitant to start a commitment to it. Then, I have come upon a verse from one of the books:<br /> <br /><i>"Oh, but it is you, darling Eve. Just as that taste is you, the smell, the look, the sound. You've undone me." </i><br /><br />- "Glory in Death"<br /><br />I think it was devastatingly beautiful! The object of Eve's undoing piqued my interest, so I went on and borrowed the first 2 books.<br /><br />"Naked in Death" is about a tough and emotionally closed-off cop called Eve Dallas, and an enigmatic billionaire called Roarke (just like "Madonna"!). In the year 2053, Eve seeks a murderer who kills prostitutes with vintage hand guns. The only lead is the last person to see the first victim alive: the aforementioned Roarke, who also owns the building she lived in, and who also has a collection of antique guns. Whom Eve shared an instant and unexplainable attraction with the moment they met. Roarke, who crumpled my expectations into a ball, and hurled it at my face! Now you'll have a sense of where I'm going with this...<br /><br />I really wanted to like him, since his dialogue is the reason I've picked up the series in the first place. Unfortunately, all this book did was make me hate him with a burning passion. He’s over-privileged, controlling and manipulative. He constantly undermines Eve’s decisions under the guise of “wanting what’s best for her”. He breaks into her apartment and invades her personal space just because he can. He throws a giant hissy fit when Eve brings him in for questioning because he’s pissed that she doesn’t trust him (even though they’ve known each other for less than a month and have only interacted a handful of times). But we’re supposed to be ok with all of his actions because he’s rich and sexy and will do anything for Eve. It’s flattering to imagine an Adonis, who can take away all your troubles, being so enamored with you. However, this doesn’t justify his actions or make him a particularly interesting character in his own right. If Eve wasn't attracted to him, she would have slapped him with a restraining order for being a creep!<br /><br />Consequently, I found Roarke so difficult and so overpowering, I didn’t really get much of a sense of Eve as a character. I appreciate that this is a series, so it takes a bit more time with character development, but I just couldn’t get a handle on her. I understood that she was sort of into order and justice pretty much on principle, and that she was totally hot for Roarke, but I didn’t get much sense of her beyond that. Even more of a problem for me was that I also didn’t get much of a sense of her being good at her job. I’m just about willing to give her a pass on having sex with the guy who is basically her only suspect (although I think it's grossly unprofessional!), but what I’m less able to reconcile is the fact that she basically doesn’t actually solve the murders at all. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She finally works out who the killer is only when somebody literally calls her up and tells her. An event which could perfectly well have happened at any time. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I apologize for the lengthy character analyses. Let me make up for them with these curt plot criticisms (I'm tired!): As a thriller, it's kinda lackluster. As a romance, it's kinda underdeveloped. As smut, it's blazingly hot! <br /><br />As is so often the case, I do wonder how much of my trouble here is to do with this being the first book in a series. There’s clearly a lot to establish and despite my issues, I plan to continue reading these books to see how the characters develop and to enjoy the gritty futuristic world Robb has built.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6058538640293269374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11532993561858092230">Hey, if you're interested in starting a fifty book series (yes, that's <u>50</u>), this one is only $2.99 on Kindle.<br/><br/>Previous post:<br/>I finally get to cross this one off my TBR shelf - and I quite enjoyed it!! :)<br/><br/>For being written in the 90s, this holds up pretty darn well.   <span id="freeText11532993561858092230" style="display:none">Hey, if you're interested in starting a fifty book series (yes, that's <u>50</u>), this one is only $2.99 on Kindle.<br /><br />Previous post:<br />I finally get to cross this one off my TBR shelf - and I quite enjoyed it!! :)<br /><br />For being written in the 90s, this holds up pretty darn well. In a way, there may not be a whole lot of uniqueness going on - it's a cop murder mystery - but it flows quite well and kept my interest. I grew to like Eve, the police lieutenant, and Roarke, the roguish millionaire (billionaire?) who is more complicated and interesting than he first appears.<br /><br />I am definitely interested in continuing the series. It's only a tiny bit "sci-fi," as it takes place in the near-future (maybe 50 years from now). There isn't any techno babble and it's all on-planet. I would barely consider this sci-fi, actually. <br /><br />But it was an enjoyable read. Roarke is a sexy male lead and Eve grew on me. <br /><br />The subject matter of this one is pretty dark (sexual murders), but it isn't too graphic. The sex was steamy enough for me, but not smutty. <br /><br />I think this was an *excellent* example of a strong female character who wasn't written into a damsel in distress role. I appreciate that. <br /><br /><b>Buddy read with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo group</a>.</b></span>

<div id="review_727013257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727013257" />
    <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish"><img alt="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398981306p2/1113032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727013257?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781593558277" href="/book/show/1542550.Naked_in_Death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=first-in-series-trilogy-duet">first-in-series-trilogy-duet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=bloody-gory-gruesome">bloody-gory-gruesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=great-supporting-cast">great-supporting-cast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=murder-mystery-whodunit">murder-mystery-whodunit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=must-read-author">must-read-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=library-audio-book">library-audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=5-stars-or-higher">5-stars-or-higher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=detective-cop">detective-cop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727013257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5820547701974846473"><br/><b>Spectacular!!!</b><br/><br/> <b>5 stars!<br/><br/> No, wait! <i>5+++++</i> Amazing, Thrilling, Provocative Stars!</b><br/><br/><b>The Story - </b><br/><br/><i>Naked in Death</i> is the first book in J.D. Robb’s insanely popular <i>In Death</i> series. It’s a fantastic mystery thriller and once I started, I couldn't put it down...errr...turn it off! <blockquote>It is the year 2058, and technology now completely rules the world. But New York City Detective Eve Dallas knows that the irresistible impulses of the human heart are still ruled by just one thing-passion. <br/><br/>When a senator's daugh</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5820547701974846473" style="display:none"><br /><b>Spectacular!!!</b><br /><br /> <b>5 stars!<br /><br /> No, wait! <i>5+++++</i> Amazing, Thrilling, Provocative Stars!</b><br /><br /><b>The Story - </b><br /><br /><i>Naked in Death</i> is the first book in J.D. Robb’s insanely popular <i>In Death</i> series. It’s a fantastic mystery thriller and once I started, I couldn't put it down...errr...turn it off! <blockquote>It is the year 2058, and technology now completely rules the world. But New York City Detective Eve Dallas knows that the irresistible impulses of the human heart are still ruled by just one thing-passion. <br /><br />When a senator's daughter is killed, the secret life of prostitution she'd been leading is revealed. The high-profile case takes Lieutenant Eve Dallas into the rarefied circles of Washington politics and society. Further complicating matters is Eve's growing attraction to Roarke, who is one of the wealthiest and most influential men on the planet, devilishly handsome... and the leading suspect in the investigation.</blockquote>I’m not usually a fan of the Mystery/Thriller genre, but my daughter has been raving about these books for years. While at the public library perusing their audio book collection I came across <i>Naked in Death,</i> and with 4.12 stars after 57,000 ratings, I decided to give it a try. <b>
  <i>WOW! I am so, so very glad I did!</i>
</b><br /><br />The world Ms. Robb has created is just futuristic enough to be compelling and believable, but not so complex as to intimidate or turn off those amongst us who are not fans of SciFi. The cast of characters, especially - be still my heart - Roarke, and Eve, are so well developed, so fully fleshed out, that I felt as if I knew them. As if they were people who were somehow part of my life. I wasn't just listening to a story, I was there as the story unfolded!<br /><br /><b>The Audio - </b><br /><br />I’ll admit that I’m fairly new to audio books, but I know what I like and what I don’t. I didn’t like this - <i>
  <b>I. Loved. It!!!</b>
</i> Susan Ericksen does a phenomenal job of bringing the cast to life. She’s an incredible talent and gives each player a distinctive voice and personality. Honestly, only one word describes her narrative skills. <i>
  <b>BRILLIANT!</b>
</i><br /><br />I need to mention, though, that while there is some romance and relationship building between the mysterious, sexy, drool-worthy Roarke, and Eve, this is first and foremost a murder mystery.<br /><br /><b>Updated here: </b> I've changed my mind! This is an amazing romance! Maybe it was because I'm not used to reading stories with so much genuinely plausible violence, that essence of the story stood out more than the romance. But now that I'm doing a re-listen while waiting for book 2, and focusing more on Roarke and Eve, there's no way there is just "some romance and relationship building." It's off the charts!<br /><br /><b>The Bottom Line - </b><br /><br />If you’re a fan of whodunits, you need to get this book. If you enjoy stories that have a futuristic element without space wars with little green men, you need to get this book. If you’re looking for something different from your usual reads, something to get you out of a reading slump, you need to get this book! You know what? Just get this book. Whether you're going to read or listen, <i>
  <b>JUST. GET. THIS. BOOK!!! </b>
</i><br /><br />There are not enough words to describe how outstanding and entertaining this book is. Intriguing, exciting, captivating, sexy… absolutely <i>
  <b>incredible!</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5820547701974846473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_305822295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305822295" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305822295?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399151576" href="/book/show/268602.Naked_in_Death">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305822295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1873024105208070425">I had never read a single book in this series. Fans know there are a great many of them now. I read the synopis on the back of the book and was instantly put off by the futuristic setting. I really don't like Science fiction and anything set in the future. History is my big thing. But, I kept hearing how good these books were, so I picked up a used copy of the first one and could not put it down. <br/>Now, if you have read Nora Roberts and think this is some extension of her other stuff, think again.</span>
  <span id="freeText1873024105208070425" style="display:none">I had never read a single book in this series. Fans know there are a great many of them now. I read the synopis on the back of the book and was instantly put off by the futuristic setting. I really don't like Science fiction and anything set in the future. History is my big thing. But, I kept hearing how good these books were, so I picked up a used copy of the first one and could not put it down. <br />Now, if you have read Nora Roberts and think this is some extension of her other stuff, think again. I was shocked by the language and the just little bit of kink thrown in there. I couldn't believe this was the same author. ( It wasn't over done, just not her style when writing as Nora Roberts.) But, when you stripped it bare, it was a detective/crime drama set in the future with a little romance thrown in for good measure. I hear maybe Roarke makes a return in her next installment. I sure hope so. <br />Eve Dallas is a take no prisoners detective. She can't remember anything before her eighth birthday. But, has memory flashes that hint at abuse. Eve would rather not remember. When a "paid companion" is murdered, her prominent family wants Eve to investigate. One of her first suspects is a billionare that was seen having dinner with the victim. Then two more women are killed. Corruption within the force,politics, lies, blackmail and murder. It's all there. Plus, Eve is finally able to start dealing with her own troubled past.If you haven't read these books, I highly recommend giving them a try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1873024105208070425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1680085581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1680085581" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1680085581?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680085581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9881673493155549662">This is a book that was written over 20 years ago, but is set in the future. And, you can tell. I don't know why, but it just feels like it was written a while back.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466982091i/19537520.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>great prediction, Jetsons. It's called a "roomba" and doesn't wear an apron..</i><br/><br/>But, I still liked all of the futuristic stuff in the story - it was fun! There was the "AutoChef" that made you food, a floating mattress - I'm thinking that would be soft and comfy, flying cars - I've been waiting forever for one of these!, tubes of Pepsi </span>
  <span id="freeText9881673493155549662" style="display:none">This is a book that was written over 20 years ago, but is set in the future. And, you can tell. I don't know why, but it just feels like it was written a while back.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466982091i/19537520.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>great prediction, Jetsons. It's called a "roomba" and doesn't wear an apron..</i><br><br>But, I still liked all of the futuristic stuff in the story - it was fun! There was the "AutoChef" that made you food, a floating mattress - I'm thinking that would be soft and comfy, flying cars - I've been waiting forever for one of these!, tubes of Pepsi - I don't know why tube-form is better but I want one, and "people movers" like elevators that move horizontally -appealing to my lazy side. Just tons of fun gadgets.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466982091i/19537521._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>gimme, gimme, gimme!</i><br><br>The story itself is about a female cop named Eve who is trying to find a serial killer. Most of the mystery is pretty good, even though I thought the bad-guy was obvious. I think it's all of the futuristic stuff that makes it more interesting. Eve was a pretty good character, but a little on the boring side. Which brings me to the romance.<br><br>Why? Why would a gorgeous billionaire fall for Eve? It happens all of the time in books. We have a dowdy, boring female who is suddenly thought to be the most desirable female on Earth to a guy who would never look at someone like her twice. Is it that authors assume us bookworms must be dowdy and boring ourselves so we are all aflutter with the idea that we could get a man like that? Cuz, dowdy and boring doesn't describe me or any of my friends here. We are are exciting and hot-stuff that a billionaire model would be LUCKY to meet!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466982091i/19537522.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, our amazingly alpha hot guy falls so fast for Eve that it's mind-boggling. He finds her lack of a sense of humor charming and the fact that she only thinks about her job adorable.<br><br>When she asks him for a favor by hacking into someone's bank account so that she can solve the crime, it rubs her rule-abiding self the wrong way:<br><b>
  <i><br>"A nonregistered system is in violation of Code four fifty-three-B, section thirty five."<br><br>"I can't tell you how aroused it makes me when you quote codes, lieutenant."<br><br>"It's not funny. And, what I'm going to ask you to do is illegal..."<br><br>"You could arrest both of us afterward."<br><br>"This is serious, Roarke..."</i>
</b><br><br>See? Isn't she delightful? He makes jokes and she keeps telling him it's not funny. As a person who makes jokes, married to the king of jokers, and with kids who are constantly joking, I can safely say that we just <i>love</i> people with no sense of humor that tell us we aren't funny when we are messing around. Yeah, they're great...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466982091i/19537523.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>But, other than the fact that I found the romance hard to believe, I still enjoyed this book. I like a good stabby-murder book, and I like future stuff - like my friends who live in Australia, so it was a win.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9881673493155549662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth"><img alt="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487525094p2/13870608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1202576421?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth">Jo ★The Book Sloth★</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=insta-love-lust">insta-love-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=like-a-virgin">like-a-virgin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=my-precious">my-precious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=mystery-suspense-crime">mystery-suspense-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1202576421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9011323148289841195"><b>5 I Should Have Read This Sooner Stars</b><br/><br/>So, I started this book 4 days ago and now I'm already reading book 4 so you can guess that I loved this, the book and the series so far.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424548597ra/13775947.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The first book was great. It had everything, a kick-ass heroine with a bad past, a powerful, slightly shady and richer than Midas hero, a great mystery and a serial killer, all that set in a futuristic world which was surprisingly well thought and realistic for a book written 20 years ago when even cell phones were a rarity</span>
  <span id="freeText9011323148289841195" style="display:none"><b>5 I Should Have Read This Sooner Stars</b><br><br>So, I started this book 4 days ago and now I'm already reading book 4 so you can guess that I loved this, the book and the series so far.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424548597ra/13775947.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first book was great. It had everything, a kick-ass heroine with a bad past, a powerful, slightly shady and richer than Midas hero, a great mystery and a serial killer, all that set in a futuristic world which was surprisingly well thought and realistic for a book written 20 years ago when even cell phones were a rarity. Also, despite the Sci-fi setting JD Robb does not make the mistake of overwhelming the reader with too much information about the discoveries and changes over the years. The world-building is smooth, with just enough details for the reader to coprehend what everything that's mentioned is but not enough to get fed up with info.<br><br>The mystery aspect of the novel was quite good. I had a new suspect every few pages, and still managed to be surprised when I found out who it was. I also loved how the author managed to write a book who was basically full of investigative work and not make it boring. To be honest, I've gotten used to UF where you have plenty of fights and magic to make the book more interesting so I wasn't sure if a good old suspense would do the trick. No fear there anymore.<br><br>My one tiny objection was on the romance side. Although I do love Roarke and Eve together, I thought the romance progressed way too fast. The series already has 40 books and no end in sight, so it could afford to prolong the "falling in love" a little. A little more tension and reluctance would have made it more believable and less mushy. Still, that wasn't enough to make me reduce the rating.<br><br>******************************************************<br><br>This book comes highly recommended from plenty of friends and my only GR friend who didn't like it was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">daddy</a>, which really is more of a recommendation than anything else <i>*bats eyes innocently*</i>, so...book you better be good!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384571209ra/6905140.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9011323148289841195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon"><img alt="♥Sharon♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1210409351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17742085573036783801"><br/>Even better the second time around! LOVED LOVED LOVED it. ❤️<br/><br/><br/><br/>❤️❤️I’ve been missing these two. Going back to the beginning of a series that I <b>LOVE</b>. ❤️❤️<br/><br/>************<br/><br/>I loved <b>Naked in Death</b> which is book #1 in the <b>In Death Series by J.D. Robb</b>. As I write this I can say I loved book #2 as well (I’ll be writing a short review soon). And I am on to book #3 and loving it already. A lot of love going on here but rightfully so. I sure hope it continues through the 40 or so books within this series. YES I s</span>
  <span id="freeText17742085573036783801" style="display:none"><br>Even better the second time around! LOVED LOVED LOVED it. ❤️<br><br><br><br>❤️❤️I’ve been missing these two. Going back to the beginning of a series that I <b>LOVE</b>. ❤️❤️<br><br>************<br><br>I loved <b>Naked in Death</b> which is book #1 in the <b>In Death Series by J.D. Robb</b>. As I write this I can say I loved book #2 as well (I’ll be writing a short review soon). And I am on to book #3 and loving it already. A lot of love going on here but rightfully so. I sure hope it continues through the 40 or so books within this series. YES I said 40!! I am anxious to see how J.D. Robb will pull off keeping her readers engaged. <br><br>I will say the writing is fantastic. The characters are intriguing and fascinating. The plot had depth and she kept me guessing almost to the end. I found that I enjoyed the fact that it is set in the future. Very clever. I’m also interested in the side characters as well. A butler of sorts, a friend and a co-worker are all subtle threads adding in peculiarities of their own. In a lengthy series like this I think it is so important the surround he H &amp; h with such characters.<br><br>I instantly fell in love with Lieutenant Eve Dallas our heroine. She is a woman of many layers. Eve is very tough on the exterior and maybe even a little tougher on the interior. But there are the moments where we see the slightest crack in her armor and get a glimpse at someone a little softer and with a sense of humor. Eve very rarely lets anything or anyone come between her and the case she is working on. It would be a first for her when she finds herself succumbing to a man. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480449531i/21312450._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This man I mention is Roarke. When he becomes a suspect in the murder case she is working on we find Eve in a bit of a predicament. Being a wealthy, sexy and handsome man doesn’t make her job easy. She would never do anything to compromise the job she has to do but the attraction she feels for him becomes almost too much to fight. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480449670i/21312470._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The murders are a bit gruesome and a tad creepy. I was completely enthralled with everything that was going on. From the suspects to the weapon to what was driving this person to kill. It was crazy!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480449725i/21312472.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This one was definitely a winner for me. As I said I have moved on and I am still enjoying this series. For all of you that enjoy RS get to this series soon.</span>
