<div id="review_58412425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58412425" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58412425?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of mystery with romance </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=very-dark-read">very-dark-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=noir-crime-mystery">noir-crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-in-pursuit">hero-in-pursuit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=all-things-winter-challenge">all-things-winter-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2011-reading">2011-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=irish-welsh-or-celtic-hero">irish-welsh-or-celtic-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-i-loved">hero-i-loved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58412425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6290334355193608294">I liked this as a mystery just as much as I liked it as a romance. Love a good mystery that keeps me guessing. I had my ideas about who the culprit was, and I was more or less right, although I had that kernel of doubt. I liked how this was a very well-plotted mystery. I think that it helped that the underlying aspects were so dark that I didn't think the story would go there. <br/><br/>Eve is a great protagonist. She's tough, intelligent, but vulnerable in some ways. She's a very good cop, and she goes a</span>
  <span id="freeText6290334355193608294" style="display:none">I liked this as a mystery just as much as I liked it as a romance. Love a good mystery that keeps me guessing. I had my ideas about who the culprit was, and I was more or less right, although I had that kernel of doubt. I liked how this was a very well-plotted mystery. I think that it helped that the underlying aspects were so dark that I didn't think the story would go there. <br /><br />Eve is a great protagonist. She's tough, intelligent, but vulnerable in some ways. She's a very good cop, and she goes after justice, and she's refreshingly down-to-earth. I can identify with the fact that she lets work take over her life, and I'm glad that Rourke is there to make that harder for her to do that. <br /><br />Speaking of Rourke....He was nice...real nice. Of course, I'm understating the case. I like that he didn't let Eve's issues stand in the way of their relationship, but he wasn't out to change her or remake her into a more manageable woman for his life. What attracted him to her was what he continued to admire about her. I love a guy who isn't afraid of a strong woman. I like how he's very supportive and caring for her, and he can get tough with her emotionally when it's necessary. If he wasn't able to, he never would have made it past the titanium barriers she keeps up. He gave up off a good future husband vibe loud and clear. It cracked me up that every time they would look up information on a company, Rourke owned it. I think his net worth should be more than 3.8 billion, since he owns pretty much everything. He's like a Harlequin Presents hero, the billionaire businessman who is too hot to resist. Rourke's larger than life personality and his developing relationship with Eve made an appreciated counterbalance to the mystery involving horrible misogyny and violence against women. Even in the future, things didn't change that much. The same forces at work in the present world are involved, hiding their ugliness behind a squeaky clean facade.<br /><br />I liked the futuristic elements. They were well-written and believable, but they weren't distracting to the mystery elements. Used very well to give me a good visual of the setting. And since I love noir mixed with most genres, the future noir in this book went over great for me.<br /><br />I can't say I'm a big Nora Roberts fan, but I definitely like this series, and I want to read more of them. I won't commit to almost forty books/stories, just yet, but I think I can agree to the next several. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6290334355193608294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776652267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2927564125173173945">I have been intending to start this series for such a long time and finally I did and boy what a start it was. I can now fully understand why this has been such a popular series. <br/><br/>Naked in Death had all the mystery, suspense, crime and intrigue that you would want with twist and turns that kept me turning the pages rather quickly. I can’t wait to read the next book in the series. Highly recommended. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2770738055530920654"><b> 2 stars </b><br/><br/>Unfortunately this book just wasn't for me. It started out strong, but by the last 100 pages I no longer cared what happened to the characters. I've never been a huge Nora Robert's fan, I find her romance too cheesy/formulaic for my taste. But I wanted to give this series a chance.<br/>I happen to be in a reading/reviewing slump, it's hard for me to review book that were just "meh" for me. So I'm going to break this down.<br/><br/>What didn't work:<br/>-the plot: it was all over the place, half romance hal</span>
  <span id="freeText2770738055530920654" style="display:none"><b> 2 stars </b><br /><br />Unfortunately this book just wasn't for me. It started out strong, but by the last 100 pages I no longer cared what happened to the characters. I've never been a huge Nora Robert's fan, I find her romance too cheesy/formulaic for my taste. But I wanted to give this series a chance.<br />I happen to be in a reading/reviewing slump, it's hard for me to review book that were just "meh" for me. So I'm going to break this down.<br /><br />What didn't work:<br />-the plot: it was all over the place, half romance half murder mystery. It never really settled<br />-INSTALOVE<br />-poorly written sex scenes <br />-poorly written "romantic scenes"<br />-murder mystery pushed into subplot in 2nd half of book<br /><br />AND (don't kill me ladies)<br /><br />...I didn't like Roarke.<br /><br />Maybe I just was anticipating too much from him? All he had going was he was rich, hot and into Eve. That was about it.<br /><br />..........................................................................<br /><br />What I liked about the book:<br />-Eve: a very complex, strong female character that is well written. I just wish she was in a better book. Maybe one day I'll pick up another one in this series as there are like 47 of them.<br /><br />So this was just an okay read for me, but I'm glad I read it. I can totally see the appeal but it doesn't appeal to me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13786289792800086735"><b>4 stars!</b><br/><br/><b>So this a 40 plus</b> book series with the same couple! Yup! I think I lost my mind since I rarely even finish a trilogy! But I can’t help myself it seems since, it’s Nora Roberts we’re talking about. <br/><br/>Anyway as far as book one goes I loved it! In till I started reading this one I hadn’t realize that this is a futuristic series which for me made it even better. <br/><br/>We have detective Eve Dallas, who is investigating the death of the senator daughter’s. During the investigation she meets the gorgeo</span>
  <span id="freeText13786289792800086735" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!</b><br /><br /><b>So this a 40 plus</b> book series with the same couple! Yup! I think I lost my mind since I rarely even finish a trilogy! But I can’t help myself it seems since, it’s Nora Roberts we’re talking about. <br /><br />Anyway as far as book one goes I loved it! In till I started reading this one I hadn’t realize that this is a futuristic series which for me made it even better. <br /><br />We have detective Eve Dallas, who is investigating the death of the senator daughter’s. During the investigation she meets the gorgeous billionaire and mysterious Roarke, too bad his also a suspect or is he?! <br /><br />I really liked how the plot played out, the suspense, the romance as far as h goes I don’t have a favorite kind as long as she goes well with story I really don’t care much. But Eve, she was amazing tough, (considering her past) independent who took her detective job as the most important thing in her life. My man Rourke of course was the perfect match for Eve he definitely brought out her vulnerable side. I like that he pushed and she pulled it wasn’t anything frustrating or OTT I say it was just right for their personalities. Their relationship wasn’t rushed.<br /><br />As for the suspense it definitely was a shocker and kinda of disturbing. Overall a solid read let’s see <b>what book two brings.</b> ♥️</span>

  <span id="freeText4289299014953157274" style="display:none">Suspense – 5 stars / Romance – 3 stars<br /><br />What could I say about this book to sound fancy?<br />Nothing. You said it all.<br /><br />Why did I wait so long to start this series? -&gt; How original?..<br />I can’t believe this book was written more than 20 years ago! -&gt; Never heard it before?<br /><br />Blah blah blah<br /><br />I liked it. Crime and suspense were written brilliantly. <br />I cracked the secret/suspense at approx.. 60% *pat myself on the back* <br /><br />As to the romance part – I’m not sure. <br />I expected the heroine being bigger badass, and I imagined the hero to be different. <br />I didn’t like Roarke. Maybe because I got almost none deep information about his personality and his past. He was enigma, slightly annoying enigma. <br />I hope he’ll come around.<br /><br />Blah blah blah<br /><br />Gotta go… I have another 18745 books in this series… Or was it more?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4289299014953157274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer713446351482697479">This is a reread for me but the last time I read it was probably 1998 or thereabouts. It was such a delight to read it again. When <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb' title='J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.D. Robb</a> wrote this first book in what was then going to be just a trilogy I wonder if she had any idea of what she had created. 40 or so books later we all feel we own a little bit of Eve and Roarke and their amazing world and we are always waiting for more!<br/>I love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/479309.Naked_in_Death__In_Death___1_' title='Naked in Death (In Death, #1) by J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Naked in Death</a>. It introduces us to our two most important characters, begins their delightful relatio</span>
  <span id="freeText713446351482697479" style="display:none">This is a reread for me but the last time I read it was probably 1998 or thereabouts. It was such a delight to read it again. When <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb" title="J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">J.D. Robb</a> wrote this first book in what was then going to be just a trilogy I wonder if she had any idea of what she had created. 40 or so books later we all feel we own a little bit of Eve and Roarke and their amazing world and we are always waiting for more!<br />I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/479309.Naked_in_Death__In_Death___1_" title="Naked in Death (In Death, #1) by J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">Naked in Death</a>. It introduces us to our two most important characters, begins their delightful relationship and sets the scene in a fascinating futuristic world. Some of the side characters also appear in this first book and we begin to discover the awful past which is Eve's driving force. I know the story well but still reached for the tissues when Eve disclosed some of her history to Roarke. Must not forget the fact that this is a crime novel and as well as romance there is a great story line and a mystery to be solved. I loved every minute of it the first time round and I loved it again this time.</span>

<div id="review_2423879154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2423879154" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2423879154?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781597105262" href="/book/show/16615679-naked-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423879154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11979615896747067934">Reread on audio. I read this book back when it was first released and as I started the audio I quickly realized my memory is not at all good! I wonder if it'll live up to my painfully vague memories of it?<br/><br/>Later:<br/><br/>I read this when was it first released in 1995 and decided to give it a reread on audio hoping it would hold up so many, many years later. 23 years later, actually! How did that happen? This book is older than my kids. Older, probably, than a few of my friends here too! Obviously, I remem</span>
  <span id="freeText11979615896747067934" style="display:none">Reread on audio. I read this book back when it was first released and as I started the audio I quickly realized my memory is not at all good! I wonder if it'll live up to my painfully vague memories of it?<br /><br />Later:<br /><br />I read this when was it first released in 1995 and decided to give it a reread on audio hoping it would hold up so many, many years later. 23 years later, actually! How did that happen? This book is older than my kids. Older, probably, than a few of my friends here too! Obviously, I remembered nothing about it except that I loved it, that it was set in the future, had a damaged heroine named Eve and that her lover was named Roarke and his past was shady. I was all into characters with dubious pasts back then, still am, I guess. I read a few more in the series before getting side-tracked by life and forgetting about it which is pretty much the story of my reading life with any series be they short or eternal like this one.<br /><br />I feared Naked In Death might not be nearly as great as I had remembered but miraculously that wasn’t the case. It’s gritty from the get-go and very murder mystery/crime procedural-ish in the most interesting of ways. I think any reader picking this up so late in the game can still enjoy it. It doesn’t feel dated and is so much better than some of the more recent Nora Roberts book I’ve read more recently. I was thinking maybe my tastes had changed but now I’m thinking Nora Robert’s has just written a few duds. Vision in White &amp; Shadow Spell? I’m talking about YOU.<br /><br />There’s no sense in rehashing the plot of this old book. I’ll just leave you with the good and the not-so-good. The chemistry and dialogue are great, there are the beginnings of some amazing character development which will continue into at least the next few books and I enjoyed reliving Eve and Rourke’s early days. <br /><br />The downside? There is insta-lust and it takes over Eve’s common sense. I won’t say anything else because its spoiler territory but if you read it you’ll see what I mean. There are also some brutal as hell death scenes, all of a sexual nature, and flashbacks of child abuse by a sexual predator. Lots of death and lots of awful sexual stuff. Be careful if these scenarios haunt you because Robb doesn’t pull any punches here.<br /><br />I’d give this book a four and ½. It’s not quite the five I remembered but I’m old and crabby now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11979615896747067934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11394047906631710028">Reading this was way way out of my comfort zone of usual reads and...I think that was a big reason why I enjoyed it too. Just something different! I've watched a lot of crimey/murdery shows but never actually read a book like it. Am doing something DIFFERENT HERE. Also I liked how it's set in 2058, the futuristic differences are subtle but cool, and totally terrifying because I suppose 2058 isn't that far away. [goes away to die quietly]<br/><br/>Basically we follow Eve Dallas who is a badass detective/co</span>
  <span id="freeText11394047906631710028" style="display:none">Reading this was way way out of my comfort zone of usual reads and...I think that was a big reason why I enjoyed it too. Just something different! I've watched a lot of crimey/murdery shows but never actually read a book like it. Am doing something DIFFERENT HERE. Also I liked how it's set in 2058, the futuristic differences are subtle but cool, and totally terrifying because I suppose 2058 isn't that far away. [goes away to die quietly]<br /><br />Basically we follow Eve Dallas who is a badass detective/cop and is on a case for the murder of several sex workers and a clever serial killer. I CALLED THE MURDERER, but not the final twist. Eve has a lot of baggage that she isn't unpacking, but I am surprised we got all her backstory here?! Aren't there like 50 books?? Thought it would've drawn more things out. The romance with Roarke was steamy and he's very suave and arrogant, but I felt he was at least somewhat still polite. I'm interested to find out his backstory tbh although he's probably a criminal and Eve will have to arrest him (again) and it will be all very angsty. 😌Me: *predicts the next 10 books at least* ANYWAY. I may read more in this series yet.<br /><br />I did find the writing too impersonal? Compared to the styles I'm used to. But it was easy to read, accessible, intriguing, and nicely-paced. Also the murder scenes are gnarlyyy.<br /><br />I finally read a book by Nora Roberts!!! The famous prolific (MACHINE?!?! how does she have so many books??!?!) writer!!!</span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catherine by: </span>

  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113420435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8033362822443586051"><b>*Originally read 12/10/10 - 12/11/10*</b><br/><br/>I've known about this series for quite a while, and I'm a big <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts' title='Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts</a> fan, but I hadn't really wanted to pick this series up. There's about a billion books out in the series. What if I ended up loving it? Then I have to commit myself to buying those billion books just to catch up! But after hearing such glowing things about this series from most of my Goodreads friends--especially about Roarke--I had to finally bight the bullet and get the first book. <br/><br/>No</span>
  <span id="freeText8033362822443586051" style="display:none"><b>*Originally read 12/10/10 - 12/11/10*</b><br /><br />I've known about this series for quite a while, and I'm a big <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" title="Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts</a> fan, but I hadn't really wanted to pick this series up. There's about a billion books out in the series. What if I ended up loving it? Then I have to commit myself to buying those billion books just to catch up! But after hearing such glowing things about this series from most of my Goodreads friends--especially about Roarke--I had to finally bight the bullet and get the first book. <br /><br />Now that I've finished it I don't know whether to cheer or comfort my wallet. I think I'm going to have to run to the bookstore and swoop up a bunch of the next books in the series so I can get my glom on.<br /><br />I didn't connect with Roarke the way that most readers seem to, but I expect it comes with time. The relationship and attraction in this book develops pretty quickly--faster than I expected or wanted--but I can't say I expected any different seeing as this isn't actually a Romance series. Most of the focus was on the case with the romance as the side story. Luckily, I know there's plenty of time in this series for the author to develop their relationship. <br /><br />It's no hardship for me to watch their relationship develop over the course of the books since I know that they <i>are</i> together and the author didn't throw any retarded love triangles in there. So I'm willing to be patient and won't complain about the lack of a lot of depth to the relationship and characters <i>yet</i>.<br /><br />It was odd for me to read a book so similar, yet different, from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" title="Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts</a>'s usual style. The characterization, interactions, feel to the developing relationship, and writing felt the same, but the focus wasn't on the romance. I liked it. It's nice to find a new series by this author that I can glut myself on. I was a little nervous that her style would be completely different under the pseudonym, but it wasn't where it counted.<br /><br />The details about all the little futuristic gizmos weren't really explained in depth. Everything was mentioned matter-of-factly like talking to someone already familiar with the technology and world. I think some will dislike that, but I honestly preferred it. I don't mind if authors want to explain, but a detailed explanation about how the spray that seals in oils and fingerprints works is not something I personally need to know. The way it was all presented worked for me.<br /><br />The case (and Eve's background) really tugged at my heartstrings. I thought it was handled well by the author, but I still feel helplessly enraged to know stuff like that happens constantly.<br /><br />I really enjoyed seeing our timeframe discussed and researched for the case. It was fun to see the differences between that time and this one and it provided a nice opportunity for me to see where their culture differed without huge infodumps.<br /><br />Now to go get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/268601.Glory_in_Death__In_Death___2_" title="Glory in Death (In Death, #2) by J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">Glory in Death</a>... <br /><br /> <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8033362822443586051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rkRFO6TC0VumpFU7zULFdiFRqF6yf96eJmtYsip0nRjWC4Ylow4vJUmYNkd4ElkAK1cHpw3FOSu0sY5+QA2X9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nOkqKyDohZIJviebHpZbUeFkLZ05eUxNhliBjqEBPgjkpuk1JyR77OaCROerxscn62KCZIbDq/gUgldCy3g05g==')})
  }

None of the gritty darkness or frenzied action is lost in 1st to Die, although the female protagonists offer an even deeper emotional context to this suspense thriller.\n\nInspector Lindsay Boxer of the San Francisco Police Department suddenly finds herself in the middle of two horrifying situations: The first is that she\'s just learned she has an often-fatal blood disease. The second is a double homicide case she is now heading up that involves the murder of newlyweds on their wedding night. Burdened with Chris Raleigh, a new partner reassigned from the mayor\'s office, Lindsay finds that she has too much to deal with and turns to her best friend, Claire, the head ME on the case. Claire offers helpful advice and human, friendly contact amid a job filled with violence, cruelty, and fear.\n\nSoon a fledgling newspaper reporter, Cindy, makes contact with Lindsay looking for a career-making story. Although Lindsay can\'t officially comment on the case, the two women form a rapport, and Cindy joins Lindsay and Claire for their weekly meeting. When a second pair of newlyweds is murdered, and later a third, the investigation leads to a prominent crime writer, Nicholas Jenks, who has a history of spousal abuse and a predilection for kinky, dangerous sex games. With the help of an understanding assistant D.A., Jill Bernhardt, Lindsay tries to make a case against Jenks, who even had an affair with one of the slain women. Eventually Jill joins the Murder Club, and the four ladies share private interdepartmental information in an effort to track and stop the killer before he strikes again.\n\nThe major subplot -- Lindsay\'s facing up to her illness even while she learns to fall in love again -- carefully compensates for the novel\'s coarse scenes of brutality. Lindsay Boxer is\'t merely an obsessed cop trailing a maniac; she\'s also a terrified woman confronting the onslaught of disease. The story lines balance out to show us the true mettle of someone who puts the safety of others before her own.\n\nAgain, Patterson\'s skill for producing furiously paced fiction are evident as the novel breezes by rapidly. The short chapters keep the narrative leaping with increasingly taut plot elements, but there\'s an emotional commitment that makes our protagonist even more amiable and involving. 1st to Die is a novel that works as an intense series of character portraits that will leave the reader touched and delighted.\n\n--Tom Piccirilli<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7110616316216620239\" href=\"#\"
